lang="en">Lung</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/w/index.php?title=Human_lung&amp;redirect=no" title="Human lung">Human lung</a>)</span><br/>\n<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" article uses anatomical terminology; for an overview, see <a href="/wiki/Anatomical_terminology" title="Anatomical terminology">anatomical terminology</a>.</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background-color:dimgray; color: style="padding-right:0.25em"><a href="/wiki/Foundational_Model_of_Anatomy" title="Foundational Model of Anatomy">FMA</a></th><td><a class="external text" href="https://bioportal.bioontology.org/ontologies/FMA/?p=classes&amp;conceptid=http%3A%2F%2Fpurl.org%2Fsig%2Font%2Ffma%2Ffma68877" rel="nofollow">68877</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><b><i><a href="/wiki/Anatomical_terminology" title="Anatomical terminology">Anatomical terminology</a></i></b><div style="text-align: right;"><small class="noprint">[<a class="extiw" href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q7886" title="d:Q7886">edit on Wikidata</a>]</small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>lungs</b> are the primary <a href="/wiki/Organ_(anatomy)" title="Organ (anatomy)">organs</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_system" title="Respiratory system">respiratory system</a> in <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">humans</a> and many other animals including a few <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a> and some <a href="/wiki/Snail" title="Snail">snails</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammals</a> and most other <a href="/wiki/Vertebrate" title="Vertebrate">vertebrates</a>, two lungs are located near the <a href="/wiki/Vertebral_column" title="Vertebral column">backbone</a> on either side of the <a href="/wiki/Heart" title="Heart">heart</a>. Their function in the respiratory system is to extract <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth%27s_atmosphere" title="Earth\'s atmosphere">atmosphere</a> and transfer it into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bloodstream" title="Bloodstream">bloodstream</a>, and to release <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> from the bloodstream into the atmosphere, in a process of <a href="/wiki/Gas_exchange" title="Gas exchange">gas exchange</a>. <a href="/wiki/Respiration_(physiology)" title="Respiration (physiology)">Respiration</a> is driven by different <a href="/wiki/Muscle" title="Muscle">muscular systems</a> in different species. Mammals, <a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">reptiles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bird" title="Bird">birds</a> use their different <a href="/wiki/Muscle" title="Muscle">muscles</a> to support and foster <a href="/wiki/Breathing" title="Breathing">breathing</a>. In early <a href="/wiki/Tetrapod" title="Tetrapod">tetrapods</a>, air was driven into the lungs by the <a href="/wiki/Pharyngeal_muscles" title="Pharyngeal muscles">pharyngeal muscles</a> via <a href="/wiki/Buccal_pumping" title="Buccal pumping">buccal pumping</a>, a mechanism still seen in <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">amphibians</a>. In humans, the main <a href="/wiki/Muscles_of_respiration" title="Muscles of respiration">muscle of respiration</a> that drives breathing is the <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">diaphragm</a>. The lungs also provide airflow that makes vocal sounds including human <a href="/wiki/Speech" title="Speech">speech</a> possible.\n</p><p>Humans have two lungs, a right lung and a left lung. They are situated within the <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_cavity" title="Thoracic cavity">thoracic cavity</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chest" title="Chest">chest</a>. The right lung is bigger than the left, which shares space in the chest with the <a href="/wiki/Heart" title="Heart">heart</a>. The lungs together weigh approximately 1.3 kilograms (2.9&#160;lb), and the right is heavier. The lungs are part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lower_respiratory_tract" title="Lower respiratory tract">lower respiratory tract</a> that begins at the <a href="/wiki/Trachea" title="Trachea">trachea</a> and branches into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bronchi" title="Bronchi">bronchi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bronchiole" title="Bronchiole">bronchioles</a>, and which receive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air" title="Air">air</a> <a href="/wiki/Inhalation" title="Inhalation">breathed in</a> via the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conducting_zone" title="Conducting zone">conducting zone</a>. The conducting zone ends at the <a href="/wiki/Bronchiole#Terminal_bronchioles" title="Bronchiole">terminal bronchioles</a>. These divide into the <a href="/wiki/Bronchiole#Respiratory_bronchioles" title="Bronchiole">respiratory bronchioles</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Respiratory_zone" title="Respiratory zone">respiratory zone</a> which divide into <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_duct" title="Alveolar duct">alveolar ducts</a> that give rise to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microscopic" title="Microscopic">microscopic</a> <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_alveolus" title="Pulmonary alveolus">alveoli</a>, where gas exchange takes place. Together, the lungs contain approximately 2,400 kilometres (1,500&#160;mi) of airways and 300 to 500 million alveoli. Each lung is enclosed within a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pleural_sac" title="Pleural sac">pleural sac</a> which allows the <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_pleurae" title="Pulmonary pleurae">inner and outer walls</a> to slide over each other whilst <a href="/wiki/Breathing" title="Breathing">breathing</a> takes place, without much friction. This sac also divides each lung into sections called <a href="/wiki/Lobe_(anatomy)" title="Lobe (anatomy)">lobes</a>. The right lung has three lobes and the left has two. The lobes are further divided into  <a href="/wiki/Bronchopulmonary_segment" title="Bronchopulmonary segment">bronchopulmonary segments</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bronchiole#Structure" title="Bronchiole">lobules</a>. The lungs have a unique blood supply, receiving deoxygenated blood from the heart in the <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_circulation" title="Pulmonary circulation">pulmonary circulation</a> for the purposes of receiving oxygen and releasing carbon dioxide, and a separate supply of oxygenated blood to the tissue of the lungs, in the <a href="/wiki/Bronchial_circulation" title="Bronchial circulation">bronchial circulation</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Parenchyma" title="Parenchyma">tissue of the lungs</a> can be affected by a <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_disease" title="Respiratory disease">number of diseases</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lung_cancer" title="Lung cancer">lung cancer</a>. <a href="/wiki/Chronic_obstructive_pulmonary_disease" title="Chronic obstructive pulmonary disease">Chronic obstructive pulmonary disease</a> includes <a href="/wiki/Bronchitis" title="Bronchitis">chronic bronchitis</a> and previously termed emphysema, can be related to <a href="/wiki/Smoking" title="Smoking">smoking</a> or exposure to <a href="/wiki/Toxicity" title="Toxicity">harmful substances</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Coal_dust" title="Coal dust">coal dust</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asbestos" title="Asbestos">asbestos fibres</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crystal" title="Crystal">crystalline</a> <a href="/wiki/Silicon_dioxide" title="Silicon dioxide">silica</a> dust. Diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Bronchitis" title="Bronchitis">bronchitis</a> can also affect the <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_tract" title="Respiratory tract">respiratory tract</a>. Medical terms related to the lung often begin with <i>pulmo-</i>, from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>pulmonarius</i> (of the lungs) as in <a href="/wiki/Pulmonology" title="Pulmonology">pulmonology</a>, or with <i>pneumo-</i> (from <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Greek</a> &#960;&#957;&#949;&#973;&#956;&#969;&#957; "lung") as in <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a>.\n</p><p>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embryogenesis" title="Embryogenesis">embryonic development</a>, the lungs begin to develop as an outpouching of the <a href="/wiki/Foregut" title="Foregut">foregut</a>, a tube which goes on to form the upper part of the digestive system. When the lungs are formed the <a href="/wiki/Fetus" title="Fetus">fetus</a> is held in the <a href="/wiki/Amniotic_fluid" title="Amniotic fluid">fluid</a>-filled <a href="/wiki/Amniotic_sac" title="Amniotic sac">amniotic sac</a> and so they do not function to breathe. Blood is also diverted from the lungs through the <a href="/wiki/Ductus_arteriosus" title="Ductus arteriosus">ductus arteriosus</a>. <a href="/wiki/Adaptation_to_extrauterine_life#Breathing_and_circulation" title="Adaptation to extrauterine life">At birth</a> however, air begins to pass through the lungs, and the diversionary duct closes, so that the lungs can begin to respire. The lungs only fully develop in early childhood.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctext">Right lung</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Left_lung"><span class="tocnumber">1.3</span> <span class="toctext">Left lung</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Microanatomy"><span class="tocnumber">1.4</span> <span class="toctext">Microanatomy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#Respiratory_tract"><span class="tocnumber">1.5</span> <span class="toctext">Respiratory tract</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#Blood_supply"><span class="tocnumber">1.6</span> <span class="toctext">Blood supply</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Nerve_supply"><span class="tocnumber">1.7</span> <span class="toctext">Nerve supply</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Development"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Development</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#After_birth"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">After birth</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Function"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Function</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Gas_exchange"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Gas exchange</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Protection"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Protection</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Other"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Other</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Gene_and_protein_expression"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Gene and protein expression</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Clinical_significance"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Clinical significance</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Lung_function_testing"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Lung function testing</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Other_animals"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Other animals</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Birds"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Birds</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Reptiles"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Reptiles</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Amphibians"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Amphibians</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Lungfish"><span class="tocnumber">6.4</span> <span class="toctext">Lungfish</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Invertebrates"><span class="tocnumber">6.5</span> <span class="toctext">Invertebrates</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Evolutionary_origins"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Evolutionary origins</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure_of_the_human_lungs">Structure of the human lungs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lung&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Structure of the human lungs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div class="PopUpMediaTransform" <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Meet_the_lungs.webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Meet the lungs" from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khan_academy" title="Khan academy">Khan academy</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anatomy">Anatomy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lung&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Anatomy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Illu_bronchi_lungs.jpg"><img alt="Illu bronchi lungs.jpg" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="330" data-file-width="520" decoding="async" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Illu_bronchi_lungs.jpg/300px-Illu_bronchi_lungs.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Illu_bronchi_lungs.jpg/450px-Illu_bronchi_lungs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/db/Illu_bronchi_lungs.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Illu_bronchi_lungs.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div></div></div></div>\n<p>The lungs are located in the <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_cavity" title="Thoracic cavity">chest</a> on either side of the <a href="/wiki/Heart" title="Heart">heart</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Rib_cage" title="Rib cage">rib cage</a>. They are conical in shape with a narrow rounded apex at the top, and a broad concave <a href="/wiki/Base_of_lung" title="Base of lung">base</a> that rests on the convex surface of the <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">diaphragm</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAYS_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-GRAYS-1">[1]</a></sup> The apex of the lung extends into the root of the neck, reaching shortly above the level of the <a href="/wiki/Sternum" title="Sternum">sternal</a> end of the <a href="/wiki/Rib_cage#Bones" title="Rib cage">first rib</a>. The lungs stretch from close to the <a href="/wiki/Vertebral_column" title="Vertebral column">backbone</a> in the rib cage to the front of the <a href="/wiki/Thorax" title="Thorax">chest</a> and downwards from the lower part of the trachea to the diaphragm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAYS_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-GRAYS-1">[1]</a></sup> The left lung shares space with the heart, and has an indentation in its border called the <b>cardiac notch of the left lung</b> to accommodate this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Betts_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Betts-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAYS40TH_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-GRAYS40TH-3">[3]</a></sup> The front and outer sides of the lungs face the ribs, which make light indentations on their surfaces. The medial surfaces of the lungs face towards the centre of the chest, and lie against the heart, <a href="/wiki/Great_vessels" title="Great vessels">great vessels</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Carina_of_trachea" title="Carina of trachea">carina</a> where the trachea divides into the two main bronchi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAYS40TH_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-GRAYS40TH-3">[3]</a></sup>  The <b>cardiac impression</b> is an indentation formed on the surfaces of the lungs where they rest against the heart.\n</p><p>Both lungs have a central recession called the  <a href="/wiki/Root_of_the_lung" title="Root of the lung">hilum</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Root_of_the_lung" title="Root of the lung">root of the lung</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Blood_vessel" title="Blood vessel">blood vessels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bronchus" title="Bronchus">airways</a> pass into the lungs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAYS_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-GRAYS-1">[1]</a></sup> There are also <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tracheobronchial_lymph_node" title="Tracheobronchial lymph node">bronchopulmonary lymph nodes</a> on the hilum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAYS40TH_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-GRAYS40TH-3">[3]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The lungs are surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_pleurae" title="Pulmonary pleurae">pulmonary pleurae</a>. The pleurae are two <a href="/wiki/Serous_membrane" title="Serous membrane">serous membranes</a>; the outer parietal pleura lines the inner wall of the <a href="/wiki/Rib_cage" title="Rib cage">rib cage</a> and the inner visceral pleura directly lines the surface of the lungs. Between the pleurae is a <a href="/wiki/Potential_space" title="Potential space">potential space</a> called the <a href="/wiki/Pleural_cavity" title="Pleural cavity">pleural cavity</a> containing a thin layer of lubricating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pleural_fluid" title="Pleural fluid">pleural fluid</a>. Each lung is divided into lobes by the infoldings of the pleura as fissures.  The fissures are double folds of pleura that section the lungs and help in their expansion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lung_fissures_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lung_fissures-4">[4]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:right;margin-left:10px">\n<caption>Lobes and bronchopulmonary segments <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid1_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid1-5">[5]</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Right lung</th>\n<th>Left lung\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Upper</b>\n<ul><li>Apical</li>\n<li>Anterior</li>\n<li>Posterior</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Middle</dt></dl>\n<ul><li>Medial</li>\n<li>Lateral</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Lower</dt></dl>\n<ul><li>Superior</li>\n<li>Anterior</li>\n<li>Posterior</li>\n<li>Medial</li>\n<li>Lateral</li></ul>\n</td>\n<td><b>Upper</b>\n<ul><li>Anterior</li>\n<li>Apicoposterior</li></ul>\n<p><b>Lower</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Superior</li>\n<li>Anterior</li>\n<li>Posterior</li>\n<li>Medial</li>\n<li>Lateral</li></ul>\n<p><b>Lingula</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Superior</li>\n<li>Inferior</li></ul>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The main or primary bronchi enter the lungs at the hilum and initially branch into <a href="/wiki/Bronchus" title="Bronchus">secondary bronchi</a> also known as lobar bronchi that supply air to each lobe of the lung. The lobar bronchi branch into <a href="/wiki/Bronchus" title="Bronchus">tertiary bronchi</a> also known as segmental bronchi and these supply air to the further divisions of the lobes known as <a href="/wiki/Bronchopulmonary_segment" title="Bronchopulmonary segment">bronchopulmonary segments</a>. Each bronchopulmonary segment has its own (segmental) bronchus and <a href="/wiki/Artery" title="Artery">arterial supply</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Segments for the left and right lung are shown in the table.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid1_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-pmid1-5">[5]</a></sup> The segmental anatomy is useful clinically for localising disease processes in the lungs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid1_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-pmid1-5">[5]</a></sup> A segment is a discrete unit that can be surgically removed without seriously affecting surrounding tissue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harper_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Harper-7">[7]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Right_lung">Right lung</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lung&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Right lung">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The right lung has both more lobes and segments than the left. It is divided into three lobes, an upper, middle, and a lower, by two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fissures" title="Fissures">fissures</a>, one oblique and one horizontal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chaudhry_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chaudhry-8">[8]</a></sup> The upper, horizontal fissure, separates the upper from the middle lobe. It begins in the lower oblique fissure near the posterior border of the lung, and, running horizontally forward, cuts the anterior border on a level with the <a href="/wiki/Sternum" title="Sternum">sternal</a> end of the fourth <a href="/wiki/Costal_cartilage" title="Costal cartilage">costal cartilage</a>; on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediastinal" title="Mediastinal">mediastinal</a> surface it may be traced backward to the <a href="/wiki/Root_of_the_lung" title="Root of the lung">hilum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAYS_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-GRAYS-1">[1]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The lower, oblique fissure, separates the lower from the middle and upper lobes, and is closely aligned with the oblique fissure in the left lung.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAYS_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-GRAYS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lung_fissures_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lung_fissures-4">[4]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The mediastinal surface of the right lung is indented by a number of nearby structures. The heart sits in an impression called the cardiac impression. Above the hilum of the lung is an arched groove for the <a href="/wiki/Azygos_vein" title="Azygos vein">azygos vein</a>, and above this is a wide groove for the <a href="/wiki/Superior_vena_cava" title="Superior vena cava">superior vena cava</a> and right <a href="/wiki/Brachiocephalic_vein" title="Brachiocephalic vein">brachiocephalic vein</a>; behind this, and close to the top of the lung is a groove for the <a href="/wiki/Brachiocephalic_artery" title="Brachiocephalic artery">brachiocephalic artery</a>. There is a groove for the esophagus behind the hilum and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pulmonary_ligament" title="Pulmonary ligament">pulmonary ligament</a>, and near the lower part of the esophageal groove is a deeper groove for the <a href="/wiki/Inferior_vena_cava" title="Inferior vena cava">inferior vena cava</a> before it enters the heart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAYS40TH_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-GRAYS40TH-3">[3]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Left_lung">Left lung</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lung&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Left lung">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The left lung is divided into two lobes, an upper and a lower, by the oblique fissure, which extends from the <a href="/wiki/Rib" title="Rib">costal</a> to the mediastinal surface of the lung both above and below the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hilum_of_lung" title="Hilum of lung">hilum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAYS_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-GRAYS-1">[1]</a></sup> The left lung, unlike the right, does not have a middle lobe, though it does have a <a href="/wiki/Homology_(biology)" title="Homology (biology)">homologous</a> feature, a projection of the upper lobe termed the "lingula".  Its name means "little tongue". The lingula on the left serves as an anatomic parallel to the right middle lobe, with both areas being predisposed to similar infections and anatomic complications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> There are two <a href="/wiki/Bronchopulmonary_segment" title="Bronchopulmonary segment">bronchopulmonary segments</a> of the lingula: superior and inferior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAYS_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-GRAYS-1">[1]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The mediastinal surface of the left lung has a large <i>cardiac impression</i> where the heart sits. This is deeper and larger than that on the right lung, at which level the heart projects to the left.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAYS40TH_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-GRAYS40TH-3">[3]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On the same surface, immediately above the hilum, is a well-marked curved groove for  the <a href="/wiki/Aortic_arch" title="Aortic arch">aortic arch</a>, and a groove below it for the <a href="/wiki/Descending_aorta" title="Descending aorta">descending aorta</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Subclavian_artery" title="Subclavian artery">left subclavian artery</a>, a branch off the aortic arch, sits in a groove from the arch to near the apex of the lung. A shallower groove in front of the artery and near the edge of the lung, lodges the left <a href="/wiki/Brachiocephalic_vein" title="Brachiocephalic vein">brachiocephalic vein</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Esophagus" title="Esophagus">esophagus</a> may sit in a wider shallow impression at the base of the lung.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAYS40TH_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-GRAYS40TH-3">[3]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gray973.png"><img alt="The left lung" data-file-height="496" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Gray973.png/200px-Gray973.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Gray973.png/300px-Gray973.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Gray973.png/400px-Gray973.png 2x" width="200"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gray972.png"><img alt="The right lung" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Gray972.png/200px-Gray972.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Gray972.png/300px-Gray972.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Gray972.png/400px-Gray972.png 2x" width="200"/></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">The left lung (left) and right lung (right). The lobes of the lungs can be seen, and the central root of the lung is also present.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Scrollable_high-resolution_computed_tomography_images_of_a_normal_thorax" title="commons:Scrollable high-resolution computed tomography images of a normal thorax"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="228" data-file-width="320" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/High-resolution_computed_tomographs_of_a_normal_thorax_%28thumbnail%29.jpg/220px-High-resolution_computed_tomographs_of_a_normal_thorax_%28thumbnail%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/30/High-resolution_computed_tomographs_of_a_normal_thorax_%28thumbnail%29.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:High-resolution_computed_tomographs_of_a_normal_thorax_(thumbnail).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/High-resolution_computed_tomography" title="High-resolution computed tomography">High-resolution</a> <a href="/wiki/CT_scan" title="CT scan">CT scans</a> of a normal thorax, taken in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axial_plane" title="Axial plane">axial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coronal_plane" title="Coronal plane">coronal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sagittal_plane" title="Sagittal plane">sagittal planes</a>, respectively. <div class="noprint"><a class="extiw" href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Scrollable_high-resolution_computed_tomography_images_of_a_normal_thorax" title="commons:Scrollable high-resolution computed tomography images of a normal thorax">Click here to scroll through the image stacks.</a></div></div></div></div>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Microanatomy">Microanatomy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lung&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Microanatomy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lung_structure_normal.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="372" data-file-width="475" decoding="async" height="219" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Lung_structure_normal.jpg/280px-Lung_structure_normal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Lung_structure_normal.jpg/420px-Lung_structure_normal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bb/Lung_structure_normal.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lung_structure_normal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cross-sectional detail of the lung</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2311_Lung_Tissue.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1932" data-file-width="1737" decoding="async" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/2311_Lung_Tissue.jpg/200px-2311_Lung_Tissue.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/2311_Lung_Tissue.jpg/300px-2311_Lung_Tissue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/2311_Lung_Tissue.jpg/400px-2311_Lung_Tissue.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2311_Lung_Tissue.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lung tissue</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alveolus_diagram.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="312" data-file-width="418" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Alveolus_diagram.svg/200px-Alveolus_diagram.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Alveolus_diagram.svg/300px-Alveolus_diagram.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Alveolus_diagram.svg/400px-Alveolus_diagram.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alveolus_diagram.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A respiratory lobule, the functional unit of the lung</div></div></div>\n<p>The lungs are part of the lower respiratory tract, and accommodate the bronchial airways when they branch from the trachea. The lungs include the bronchial airways that terminate in <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_alveolus" title="Pulmonary alveolus">alveoli</a>, the lung <a href="/wiki/Tissue_(biology)" title="Tissue (biology)">tissue</a> in between, and veins, arteries, nerves and <a href="/wiki/Lymphatic_vessel" title="Lymphatic vessel">lymphatic vessels</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAYS40TH_3-6"><a href="#cite_note-GRAYS40TH-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The trachea and bronchi have plexuses of <a href="/wiki/Lymph_capillary" title="Lymph capillary">lymph capillaries</a> in their mucosa and submucosa. The smaller bronchi have a single layer and they are absent in the alveoli.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Theodora_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Theodora-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p><p>All of the lower respiratory tract including the trachea, bronchi, and bronchioles is lined with <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_epithelium" title="Respiratory epithelium">respiratory epithelium</a>. This is a <a href="/wiki/Cilium" title="Cilium">ciliated</a> epithelium interspersed with <a href="/wiki/Goblet_cell" title="Goblet cell">goblet cells</a> which produce <a href="/wiki/Mucus" title="Mucus">mucus</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Club_cells" title="Club cells">club cells</a> with actions similar to <a href="/wiki/Macrophage" title="Macrophage">macrophages</a>. Incomplete rings of <a href="/wiki/Cartilage" title="Cartilage">cartilage</a> in the trachea and smaller plates of cartilage in the bronchi, keep these airways open.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuytonHall_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-GuytonHall-13">[13]</a></sup> Bronchioles are too narrow to support cartilage and their walls are of <a href="/wiki/Smooth_muscle" title="Smooth muscle">smooth muscle</a>, and this is largely absent in the narrower <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Respiratory_bronchiole" title="Respiratory bronchiole">respiratory bronchioles</a> which are mainly just of epithelium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuytonHall_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-GuytonHall-13">[13]</a></sup> The respiratory tract ends in <a href="/wiki/Bronchiole#Structure" title="Bronchiole">lobules</a>. Each lobule consists of a respiratory bronchiole, which branches into <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_duct" title="Alveolar duct">alveolar ducts</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_sac" title="Alveolar sac">alveolar sacs</a>, which in turn divide into alveoli.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAYS40TH_3-7"><a href="#cite_note-GRAYS40TH-3">[3]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The epithelial cells throughout the respiratory tract secrete epithelial lining fluid (ELF), the composition of which is tightly regulated and determines how well <a href="/wiki/Mucociliary_clearance" title="Mucociliary clearance">mucociliary clearance</a> works.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAassess2016_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPAassess2016-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>Section 4 pages 7&#8211;8 (Page 4&#8211;7ff)</span></sup>\n</p><p>Alveoli consist of two types of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_cell" title="Alveolar cell">alveolar cell</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_macrophage" title="Alveolar macrophage">alveolar macrophage</a>. The two types of cell are known as type I and type II alveolar cells<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BERNELEVY_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-BERNELEVY-16">[16]</a></sup> (also known as pneumocytes).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GRAYS40TH_3-8"><a href="#cite_note-GRAYS40TH-3">[3]</a></sup> Types I and II make up the walls and <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_septum" title="Alveolar septum">alveolar septa</a>. Type I cells provide 95% of the surface area of each alveoli and are flat ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Squamous_epithelial_cell" title="Squamous epithelial cell">squamous</a>"), and Type II cells generally cluster in the corners of the alveoli and have a cuboidal shape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAWLINA_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-PAWLINA-17">[17]</a></sup> Despite this, cells occur in a roughly equal ratio of 1:1 or 6:4.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BERNELEVY_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-BERNELEVY-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAWLINA_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-PAWLINA-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Type I are <a href="/wiki/Epithelium" title="Epithelium">squamous epithelial cells</a> that make up the alveolar wall structure. They have extremely thin walls that enable an easy gas exchange.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BERNELEVY_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-BERNELEVY-16">[16]</a></sup> These type I cells also make up the alveolar septa which separate each alveolus. The septa consist of an epithelial lining and associated <a href="/wiki/Basement_membrane" title="Basement membrane">basement membranes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAWLINA_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-PAWLINA-17">[17]</a></sup> Type I cells are not able to divide, and consequently rely on <a href="/wiki/Cellular_differentiation" title="Cellular differentiation">differentiation</a> from Type II cells.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAWLINA_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-PAWLINA-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Type II are larger and they line the alveoli and produce and secrete epithelial lining fluid, and <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_surfactant" title="Pulmonary surfactant">lung surfactant</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BERNELEVY_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-BERNELEVY-16">[16]</a></sup> Type II cells are able to divide and differentiate to Type 1 cells.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAWLINA_17-4"><a href="#cite_note-PAWLINA-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The alveolar <a href="/wiki/Macrophage" title="Macrophage">macrophages</a> have an important <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">immunological</a> role. They remove substances which deposit in the alveoli including loose red blood cells that have been forced out from blood vessels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAWLINA_17-5"><a href="#cite_note-PAWLINA-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The lung is surrounded by a <a href="/wiki/Serous_membrane" title="Serous membrane">serous membrane</a> of visceral pleura, which has an underlying layer of <a href="/wiki/Loose_connective_tissue" title="Loose connective tissue">loose connective tissue</a> attached to the substance of the lung.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dorlands1077_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dorlands1077-19">[19]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Respiratory_tract">Respiratory tract</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lung&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Respiratory tract">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_tract" title="Respiratory tract">Respiratory tract</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Illu_conducting_passages.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="328" data-file-width="255" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Illu_conducting_passages.svg/130px-Illu_conducting_passages.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Illu_conducting_passages.svg/195px-Illu_conducting_passages.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Illu_conducting_passages.svg/260px-Illu_conducting_passages.svg.png 2x" width="130"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Illu_conducting_passages.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The lungs as main part of respiratory tract</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_tract#Lower_respiratory_tract" title="Respiratory tract">lower respiratory tract</a> is part of the <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_system" title="Respiratory system">respiratory system</a>, and consists of the <a href="/wiki/Trachea" title="Trachea">trachea</a> and the structures below this including the lungs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BERNELEVY_16-4"><a href="#cite_note-BERNELEVY-16">[16]</a></sup> The trachea receives air from the <a href="/wiki/Pharynx" title="Pharynx">pharynx</a> and travels down to a place where it splits (the <a href="/wiki/Carina_of_trachea" title="Carina of trachea">carina</a>) into a right and left <a href="/wiki/Bronchus" title="Bronchus">bronchus</a>. These supply air to the right and left lungs, splitting progressively into the secondary and tertiary bronchi for the lobes of the lungs, and into smaller and smaller bronchioles until they become the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Respiratory_bronchiole" title="Respiratory bronchiole">respiratory bronchioles</a>. These in turn supply air through <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_duct" title="Alveolar duct">alveolar ducts</a> into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveoli" title="Alveoli">alveoli</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Gas_exchange" title="Gas exchange">exchange of gases</a> take place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BERNELEVY_16-5"><a href="#cite_note-BERNELEVY-16">[16]</a></sup> Oxygen <a href="/wiki/Inhalation" title="Inhalation">breathed in</a>, <a href="/wiki/Molecular_diffusion#Biology" title="Molecular diffusion">diffuses</a> through the walls of the alveoli into the enveloping <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capillaries" title="Capillaries">capillaries</a> and into the <a href="/wiki/Circulatory_system" title="Circulatory system">circulation</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> and carbon dioxide diffuses from the blood into the lungs to be <a href="/wiki/Exhalation" title="Exhalation">breathed out</a>.\n</p><p>Estimates of the total surface area of lungs vary from 50 to 75 square metres (540 to 810&#160;sq&#160;ft);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BERNELEVY_16-6"><a href="#cite_note-BERNELEVY-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAWLINA_17-6"><a href="#cite_note-PAWLINA-17">[17]</a></sup> roughly the same area as one side of a <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> court.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAWLINA_17-7"><a href="#cite_note-PAWLINA-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The bronchi in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conducting_zone" title="Conducting zone">conducting zone</a> are reinforced with <a href="/wiki/Hyaline_cartilage" title="Hyaline cartilage">hyaline cartilage</a> in order to hold open the airways. The bronchioles have no cartilage and are surrounded instead by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Smooth_muscle_tissue" title="Smooth muscle tissue">smooth muscle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAWLINA_17-8"><a href="#cite_note-PAWLINA-17">[17]</a></sup>  Air is warmed to 37&#160;&#176;C (99&#160;&#176;F), <a href="/wiki/Humidity" title="Humidity">humidified</a> and cleansed by the conducting zone; particles from the air being removed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cilia" title="Cilia">cilia</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_epithelium" title="Respiratory epithelium">respiratory epithelium</a> lining the passageways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ahmadi2013_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ahmadi2013-22">[22]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pulmonary_stretch_receptor" title="Pulmonary stretch receptor">Pulmonary stretch receptors</a> in the smooth muscle of the airways initiate a <a href="/wiki/Reflex" title="Reflex">reflex</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Hering%E2%80%93Breuer_reflex" title="Hering&#8211;Breuer reflex">Hering&#8211;Breuer reflex</a> that prevents the lungs from over-inflation, during forceful inspiration.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Blood_supply">Blood supply</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lung&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Blood supply">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_circulation" title="Pulmonary circulation">Pulmonary circulation</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:3D_CT_of_thorax,_annotated.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1131" data-file-width="1544" decoding="async" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/3D_CT_of_thorax%2C_annotated.jpg/320px-3D_CT_of_thorax%2C_annotated.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/3D_CT_of_thorax%2C_annotated.jpg/480px-3D_CT_of_thorax%2C_annotated.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/3D_CT_of_thorax%2C_annotated.jpg/640px-3D_CT_of_thorax%2C_annotated.jpg 2x" width="320"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:3D_CT_of_thorax,_annotated.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/3D_rendering" title="3D rendering">3D rendering</a> of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_resolution_computed_tomography" title="High resolution computed tomography">high resolution computed tomography</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Thorax" title="Thorax">thorax</a>. The anterior thoracic wall, the airways and the pulmonary vessels anterior to the <a href="/wiki/Root_of_the_lung" title="Root of the lung">root of the lung</a> have been digitally removed in order to visualize the different levels of the <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_circulation" title="Pulmonary circulation">pulmonary circulation</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The lungs have a dual blood supply<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BERNELEVY_16-7"><a href="#cite_note-BERNELEVY-16">[16]</a></sup> provided by a <a href="/wiki/Bronchial_circulation" title="Bronchial circulation">bronchial</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_circulation" title="Pulmonary circulation">pulmonary circulation</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Bronchial_circulation" title="Bronchial circulation">bronchial circulation</a> supplies oxygenated blood to the airways of the lungs, through the <a href="/wiki/Bronchial_artery" title="Bronchial artery">bronchial arteries</a> that leave the <a href="/wiki/Aorta" title="Aorta">aorta</a>.  There are usually three arteries, two to the left lung and one to the right,  and they branch alongside the bronchi and bronchioles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BERNELEVY_16-8"><a href="#cite_note-BERNELEVY-16">[16]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_circulation" title="Pulmonary circulation">pulmonary circulation</a> carries deoxygenated blood from the heart to the lungs and returns the oxygenated blood to the heart to supply the rest of the body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BERNELEVY_16-9"><a href="#cite_note-BERNELEVY-16">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The blood volume of the lungs, is about 450 millilitres on average, about 9 per cent of the total blood volume of the entire circulatory system. This quantity can easily fluctuate from between one-half and twice the normal volume.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nerve_supply">Nerve supply</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lung&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Nerve supply">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The lungs are supplied by nerves of the <a href="/wiki/Autonomic_nervous_system" title="Autonomic nervous system">autonomic nervous system</a>. Input from the <a href="/wiki/Parasympathetic_nervous_system" title="Parasympathetic nervous system">parasympathetic nervous system</a> occurs via the <a href="/wiki/Vagus_nerve" title="Vagus nerve">vagus nerve</a>. When stimulated by <a href="/wiki/Acetylcholine" title="Acetylcholine">acetylcholine</a>, this causes constriction of the smooth muscle lining the bronchus and bronchioles, and increases the secretions from glands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Levitzky2013_2_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Levitzky2013_2-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (January 2018)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The lungs also have a sympathetic tone from <a href="/wiki/Norepinephrine" title="Norepinephrine">norepinephrine</a> acting on the <a href="/wiki/Beta-2_adrenergic_receptor" title="Beta-2 adrenergic receptor">beta 2 receptors</a> in the respiratory tract, which causes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bronchodilation" title="Bronchodilation">bronchodilation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Levitzky2013_2_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Levitzky2013_2-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (January 2018)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The action of breathing takes place because of nerve signals sent by the <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_center" title="Respiratory center">respiratory centres</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Brainstem" title="Brainstem">brainstem</a>, along the <a href="/wiki/Phrenic_nerve" title="Phrenic nerve">phrenic nerve</a> to the diaphragm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Levitzky2013_9_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Levitzky2013_9-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (January 2018)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lung&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The development of the human lungs arise from the <a href="/wiki/Laryngotracheal_groove" title="Laryngotracheal groove">laryngotracheal groove</a> and develop to maturity over several weeks in the foetus and for several years following birth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sadler_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sadler-26">[26]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Larynx" title="Larynx">larynx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trachea" title="Trachea">trachea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bronchus" title="Bronchus">bronchi</a> and lungs that make up the respiratory tract, begin to form during the fourth week of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_embryogenesis" title="Human embryogenesis">embryogenesis</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moore_2002_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Moore_2002-27">[27]</a></sup> from the <a href="/wiki/Lung_bud" title="Lung bud">lung bud</a> which appears ventrally to the caudal portion of the <a href="/wiki/Foregut" title="Foregut">foregut</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gray949.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="207" data-file-width="300" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Gray949.png/220px-Gray949.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0d/Gray949.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gray949.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lungs during development, showing the early branching of the primitive bronchial buds</div></div></div>\n<p>The respiratory tract has a branching structure like that of a tree.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miura_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Miura-29">[29]</a></sup> In the embryo this structure is developed in the process of branching <a href="/wiki/Morphogenesis" title="Morphogenesis">morphogenesis</a>, and is generated by the repeated splitting of the tip of the branch. In the development of the lungs (as in some other organs) the epithelium forms branching tubes.The lung has a left-right symmetry and each bud known as a <a href="/wiki/Lung_bud" title="Lung bud">bronchial bud</a> grows out as a tubular epithelium that becomes a bronchus. Each bronchus branches into bronchioles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolpert_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wolpert-30">[30]</a></sup> The branching is a result of the tip of each tube bifurcating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miura_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Miura-29">[29]</a></sup> The branching process forms the bronchi, bronchioles, and ultimately the alveoli.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miura_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-Miura-29">[29]</a></sup> The four genes mostly associated with branching morphogenesis in the lung are the <a href="/wiki/Hedgehog_signaling_pathway" title="Hedgehog signaling pathway">intercellular signalling protein</a> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Sonic_hedgehog" title="Sonic hedgehog">sonic hedgehog</a> (SHH), <a href="/wiki/Fibroblast_growth_factor" title="Fibroblast growth factor">fibroblast growth factors</a> <a href="/wiki/FGF10" title="FGF10">FGF10</a> and FGFR2b, and <a href="/wiki/Bone_morphogenetic_protein" title="Bone morphogenetic protein">bone morphogenetic protein</a> <a href="/wiki/Bone_morphogenetic_protein_4" title="Bone morphogenetic protein 4">BMP4</a>. FGF10 is seen to have the most prominent role. FGF10 is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paracrine_signalling" title="Paracrine signalling">paracrine signalling</a> molecule needed for epithelial branching, and SHH inhibits FGF10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miura_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-Miura-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolpert_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wolpert-30">[30]</a></sup> The development of the alveoli is influenced by a different mechanism whereby continued bifurcation is stopped and the distal tips become dilated to form the alveoli.\n</p><p>At the end of the fourth week the lung bud divides into two, the right and left <a href="/wiki/Lung_bud" title="Lung bud">primary bronchial buds</a> on each side of the trachea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Larsen2001_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Larsen2001-32">[32]</a></sup> During the fifth week the right bud branches into three secondary bronchial buds and the left branches into two secondary bronchial buds. These give rise to the lobes of the lungs, three on the right and two on the left. Over the following week, the secondary buds branch into tertiary buds, about ten on each side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Larsen2001_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-Larsen2001-32">[32]</a></sup> From the sixth week to the sixteenth week, the major elements of the lungs appear except the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolus" title="Alveolus">alveoli</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-isbn0-7817-5309-0_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-isbn0-7817-5309-0-33">[33]</a></sup> From week 16 to week 26, the bronchi enlarge and lung tissue becomes highly vascularised. Bronchioles and alveolar ducts also develop. By week 26 the terminal bronchioles have formed which branch into two respiratory bronchioles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> During the period covering the 26th week until birth the important <a href="/wiki/Blood%E2%80%93air_barrier" title="Blood&#8211;air barrier">blood&#8211;air barrier</a> is established. Specialised <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_cells" title="Alveolar cells">type I alveolar cells</a> where <a href="/wiki/Gas_exchange" title="Gas exchange">gas exchange</a> will take place, together with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_cells" title="Alveolar cells">type II alveolar cells</a> that secrete <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_surfactant" title="Pulmonary surfactant">pulmonary surfactant</a>, appear. The surfactant reduces the <a href="/wiki/Surface_tension" title="Surface tension">surface tension</a> at the air-alveolar surface which allows expansion of the alveolar sacs. The alveolar sacs contain the primitive alveoli that form at the end of the alveolar ducts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>\nand their appearance around the seventh month marks the point at which limited respiration would be possible, and the premature baby could survive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sadler_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sadler-26">[26]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_birth">After birth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lung&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: After birth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>At <a href="/wiki/Childbirth" title="Childbirth">birth</a>, the baby\'s lungs are filled with fluid secreted by the lungs and are not inflated. <a href="/wiki/Adaptation_to_extrauterine_life#Breathing_and_circulation" title="Adaptation to extrauterine life">After birth</a> the infant\'s <a href="/wiki/Central_nervous_system" title="Central nervous system">central nervous system</a> reacts to the sudden change in temperature and environment. This triggers the first breath, within about 10 seconds after delivery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Medline2015_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Medline2015-36">[36]</a></sup> Before birth, the lungs are filled with fetal lung fluid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>      After the first breath, the fluid is quickly absorbed into the body or exhaled. The <a href="/wiki/Vascular_resistance" title="Vascular resistance">resistance</a> in the lung\'s blood vessels decreases giving an increased surface area for gas exchange, and the lungs begin to breathe spontaneously. This accompanies <a href="/wiki/Adaptation_to_extrauterine_life" title="Adaptation to extrauterine life">other changes</a> which result in an increased amount of blood entering the lung tissues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Medline2015_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Medline2015-36">[36]</a></sup>\n</p><p>At birth the lungs are very undeveloped with only around one sixth of the alveoli of the adult lung present.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sadler_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sadler-26">[26]</a></sup> The alveoli continue to form into early adulthood, and their ability to form when necessary is seen in the regeneration of the lung.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schittny_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schittny-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SchittnyJC_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-SchittnyJC-39">[39]</a></sup> Alveolar septa have a double <a href="/wiki/Capillary#Structure" title="Capillary">capillary network</a> instead of the single network of the developed lung. Only after the maturation of the capillary network can the lung enter a normal phase of growth. Following the early growth in numbers of alveoli there is another stage of the alveoli being enlarged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Function">Function</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lung&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Function">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_system" title="Respiratory system">Respiratory system</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breathing" title="Breathing">Breathing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gas_exchange" title="Gas exchange">Gas exchange</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gas_exchange">Gas exchange</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lung&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Gas exchange">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The major function of the lungs is <a href="/wiki/Gas_exchange" title="Gas exchange">gas exchange</a> between the lungs and the blood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_alveolus" title="Pulmonary alveolus">alveolar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_circulation" title="Pulmonary circulation">pulmonary capillary</a> gases equilibrate across the thin <a href="/wiki/Blood%E2%80%93air_barrier" title="Blood&#8211;air barrier">blood&#8211;air barrier</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grays_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-grays-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-s-cool_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-s-cool-43">[43]</a></sup> This thin membrane (about 0.5 &#8211;2&#160;&#956;m thick) is folded into about 300 million alveoli, providing an extremely large surface area (estimates varying between 70 and 145&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) for gas exchange to occur.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grays_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-grays-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ribcage_during_inhalation.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2380" data-file-width="3003" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ribcage_during_inhalation.jpg/220px-Ribcage_during_inhalation.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ribcage_during_inhalation.jpg/330px-Ribcage_during_inhalation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ribcage_during_inhalation.jpg/440px-Ribcage_during_inhalation.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ribcage_during_inhalation.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The effect of the <a href="/wiki/Muscles_of_respiration" title="Muscles of respiration">respiratory muscles</a> in expanding the <a href="/wiki/Rib_cage" title="Rib cage">rib cage</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The lungs are not capable of expanding to <a href="/wiki/Breathing" title="Breathing">breathe</a> on their own, and will only do so when there is an increase in the volume of the thoracic cavity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Levitzky2013_1_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Levitzky2013_1-45">[45]</a></sup> This is achieved by the <a href="/wiki/Muscles_of_respiration" title="Muscles of respiration">muscles of respiration</a>, through the contraction of the <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">diaphragm</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intercostal_muscles" title="Intercostal muscles">intercostal muscles</a> which pull the <a href="/wiki/Rib_cage" title="Rib cage">rib cage</a> upwards as shown in the diagram.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> During <a href="/wiki/Exhalation" title="Exhalation">breathing out</a> the muscles relax, returning the lungs to their resting position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tortora1_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-tortora1-47">[47]</a></sup> At this point the lungs contain the <a href="/wiki/Functional_residual_capacity" title="Functional residual capacity">functional residual capacity</a> (FRC) of air, which, in the adult human, has a volume of about 2.5&#8211;3.0 litres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tortora1_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-tortora1-47">[47]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyperpnoea" title="Hyperpnoea">heavy breathing</a> as in <a href="/wiki/Exertion" title="Exertion">exertion</a>, a large number of <a href="/wiki/Muscles_of_respiration#Accessory_muscles" title="Muscles of respiration">accessory muscles</a> in the neck and abdomen are recruited, that during exhalation pull the ribcage down, decreasing the volume of the thoracic cavity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tortora1_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-tortora1-47">[47]</a></sup> The FRC is now decreased, but since the lungs cannot be emptied completely there is still about a litre of residual air left.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tortora1_47-3"><a href="#cite_note-tortora1-47">[47]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lung#Lung_function_testing" title="Lung">Lung function testing</a> is carried out to evaluate <a href="/wiki/Lung_volumes" title="Lung volumes">lung volumes</a> and capacities.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Protection">Protection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lung&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Protection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The lungs possess several characteristics which protect against infection. The respiratory tract is lined by <a href="/wiki/Epithelium" title="Epithelium">epithelia</a> with hair-like projections called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cilia" title="Cilia">cilia</a> that beat rhythmically and carry mucus. This <a href="/wiki/Mucociliary_clearance" title="Mucociliary clearance">mucociliary clearance</a> is an important defence system against air-borne infection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">[18]</a></sup> The dust particles and bacteria in the inhaled air are caught in the mucosal surface of the airways, and are moved up towards the pharynx by the rhythmic upward beating action of the cilia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAWLINA_17-9"><a href="#cite_note-PAWLINA-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DAVIDSONS2014_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-DAVIDSONS2014-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The lining of the lung also secretes <a href="/wiki/Immunoglobulin_A" title="Immunoglobulin A">immunoglobulin A</a> which protects against respiratory infections;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DAVIDSONS2014_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-DAVIDSONS2014-48">[48]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goblet_cells" title="Goblet cells">goblet cells</a> secrete mucus<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAWLINA_17-10"><a href="#cite_note-PAWLINA-17">[17]</a></sup> which also contains several antimicrobial compounds such as <a href="/wiki/Defensin" title="Defensin">defensins</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antiprotease" title="Antiprotease">antiproteases</a>, and antioxidates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DAVIDSONS2014_48-2"><a href="#cite_note-DAVIDSONS2014-48">[48]</a></sup> Ionocytes regulate mucus viscosity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In addition, the lining of the lung also contains <a href="/wiki/Macrophage" title="Macrophage">macrophages</a>, immune cells which engulf and destroy debris and microbes that enter the lung in a process known as <a href="/wiki/Phagocytosis" title="Phagocytosis">phagocytosis</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Dendritic_cell" title="Dendritic cell">dendritic cells</a> which present antigens to activate components of the <a href="/wiki/Adaptive_immune_system" title="Adaptive immune system">adaptive immune system</a> such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T-cell" title="T-cell">T-cells</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B-cell" title="B-cell">B-cells</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DAVIDSONS2014_48-3"><a href="#cite_note-DAVIDSONS2014-48">[48]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The size of the respiratory tract and the flow of air also protect the lungs from larger particles. Smaller particles deposit in the <a href="/wiki/Human_mouth" title="Human mouth">mouth</a> and behind the mouth in the <a href="/wiki/Pharynx#Oropharynx" title="Pharynx">oropharynx</a>, and larger particles are trapped in <a href="/wiki/Nasal_hair" title="Nasal hair">nasal hair</a> after inhalation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DAVIDSONS2014_48-4"><a href="#cite_note-DAVIDSONS2014-48">[48]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lung&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In addition to their function in respiration, the lungs have a number of other functions. They are involved in maintaining <a href="/wiki/Homeostasis" title="Homeostasis">homeostasis</a>, helping in the regulation of <a href="/wiki/Blood_pressure" title="Blood pressure">blood pressure</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Renin%E2%80%93angiotensin_system" title="Renin&#8211;angiotensin system">renin&#8211;angiotensin system</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Endothelium" title="Endothelium">inner lining</a> of the blood vessels secretes <a href="/wiki/Angiotensin-converting_enzyme" title="Angiotensin-converting enzyme">angiotensin-converting enzyme</a> (ACE) an <a href="/wiki/Enzyme" title="Enzyme">enzyme</a> that <a href="/wiki/Catalysis" title="Catalysis">catalyses</a> the conversion of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angiotensin_I" title="Angiotensin I">angiotensin I</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angiotensin_II" title="Angiotensin II">angiotensin II</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boron_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-boron-52">[52]</a></sup> The lungs are involved in the blood\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acid-base_homeostasis" title="Acid-base homeostasis">acid-base homeostasis</a> by expelling <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> when breathing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Levitzky2013_1_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-Levitzky2013_1-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PatientInfo_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-PatientInfo-53">[53]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The lungs also serve a protective role. Several blood-borne substances, such as a few types of <a href="/wiki/Prostaglandin" title="Prostaglandin">prostaglandins</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leukotrienes" title="Leukotrienes">leukotrienes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serotonin" title="Serotonin">serotonin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bradykinin" title="Bradykinin">bradykinin</a>, are excreted through the lungs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boron_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-boron-52">[52]</a></sup> Drugs and other substances can be absorbed, modified or excreted in the lungs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Levitzky2013_1_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-Levitzky2013_1-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smyth_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Smyth-54">[54]</a></sup> The lungs filter out small <a href="/wiki/Thrombus" title="Thrombus">blood clots</a> from <a href="/wiki/Vein" title="Vein">veins</a> and prevent them from entering <a href="/wiki/Artery" title="Artery">arteries</a> and causing <a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">strokes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PatientInfo_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-PatientInfo-53">[53]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The lungs also play a pivotal role in <a href="/wiki/Speech" title="Speech">speech</a> by providing air and airflow for the creation of vocal sounds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Levitzky2013_1_45-3"><a href="#cite_note-Levitzky2013_1-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> and other <a href="/wiki/Paralanguage" title="Paralanguage">paralanguage</a> <a href="/wiki/Paralanguage#Specific_forms_of_paralinguistic_respiration" title="Paralanguage">communications</a> such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sighing" title="Sighing">sighs</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gasp" title="Gasp">gasps</a>.\n</p><p>New research suggests a role of the lungs in the production of blood platelets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gene_and_protein_expression">Gene and protein expression</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lung&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Gene and protein expression">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Bioinformatics#Gene_and_protein_expression" title="Bioinformatics">Bioinformatics &#167;&#160;Gene and protein expression</a></div>\n<p>About 20,000 <a href="/wiki/Human_genome#Coding_sequences_(protein-coding_genes)" title="Human genome">protein coding genes</a> are expressed in human cells and almost 75% of these genes are expressed in the normal lung.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> A little less than 200 of these genes are more specifically expressed in the lung with less than 20 genes being highly lung specific. The corresponding specific proteins are expressed within different cellular compartments such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_cells" title="Alveolar cells">pneumocytes</a> in alveoli, and ciliated and mucus secreting <a href="/wiki/Goblet_cell" title="Goblet cell">goblet cells</a> in the respiratory mucosa. The highest expression of lung specific proteins are different <a href="/wiki/Surfactant" title="Surfactant">surfactant</a> proteins,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">[18]</a></sup> such as <a href="/wiki/Surfactant_protein_A1" title="Surfactant protein A1">SFTPA1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Surfactant_protein_B" title="Surfactant protein B">SFTPB</a> and <a href="/wiki/Surfactant_protein_C" title="Surfactant protein C">SFTPC</a>, and <a href="/wiki/NAPSA" title="NAPSA">napsin</a>, expressed in type II pneumocytes. Other proteins with elevated expression in the lung are the <a href="/wiki/Dynein" title="Dynein">dynein</a> protein <a href="/wiki/DNAH5" title="DNAH5">DNAH5</a> in ciliated cells, and the secreted <a href="/wiki/Uteroglobin" title="Uteroglobin">SCGB1A1</a> protein in mucus secreting  goblet cells of the airway mucosa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Clinical_significance">Clinical significance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lung&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Clinical significance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_disease" title="Respiratory disease">Respiratory disease</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pulmonology" title="Pulmonology">Pulmonology</a></div>\n<p>Lungs can be affected by a variety of diseases. <a href="/wiki/Pulmonology" title="Pulmonology">Pulmonology</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Specialty_(medicine)" title="Specialty (medicine)">medical speciality</a> that deals with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diseases" title="Diseases">diseases</a> involving the <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_tract" title="Respiratory tract">respiratory tract</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACP_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-ACP-60">[60]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Cardiothoracic_surgery" title="Cardiothoracic surgery">cardiothoracic surgery</a> is the surgical field that deals with surgery of the lungs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Inflammation" title="Inflammation">Inflammatory</a> conditions of the lung tissue are <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a>, of the respiratory tract are <a href="/wiki/Bronchitis" title="Bronchitis">bronchitis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bronchiolitis" title="Bronchiolitis">bronchiolitis</a>, and of the <a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_pleurae" title="Pulmonary pleurae">pleurae</a> surrounding the lungs <a href="/wiki/Pleurisy" title="Pleurisy">pleurisy</a>. Inflammation is usually caused by <a href="/wiki/Infection" title="Infection">infections</a> due to <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a> or <a href="/wiki/Virus" title="Virus">viruses</a>. When the lung tissue is inflamed due to other causes it is called <a href="/wiki/Pneumonitis" title="Pneumonitis">pneumonitis</a>. One major cause of <a href="/wiki/Bacterial_pneumonia" title="Bacterial pneumonia">bacterial pneumonia</a> is <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DAVIDSONS2014_48-5"><a href="#cite_note-DAVIDSONS2014-48">[48]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chronic_condition" title="Chronic condition">Chronic</a> infections often occur in those with <a href="/wiki/Immunodeficiency" title="Immunodeficiency">immunodeficiency</a> and can include a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fungal_infection" title="Fungal infection">fungal infection</a> by <i><a href="/wiki/Aspergillus_fumigatus" title="Aspergillus fumigatus">Aspergillus fumigatus</a></i> that can lead to an <a href="/wiki/Aspergilloma" title="Aspergilloma">aspergilloma</a> forming in the lung.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DAVIDSONS2014_48-6"><a href="#cite_note-DAVIDSONS2014-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:InfarctPandLbasilarsegmentsPE.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="838" data-file-width="1094" decoding="async" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/InfarctPandLbasilarsegmentsPE.PNG/240px-InfarctPandLbasilarsegmentsPE.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/InfarctPandLbasilarsegmentsPE.PNG/360px-InfarctPandLbasilarsegmentsPE.PNG 1.5x,
